</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://meekmill.com">meekmill<wbr />.com</a></span>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Robert Rihmeek Williams</b> (born May 6, 1987),<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> known professionally as <b>Meek Mill</b>, is an American rapper. 
</p><p>Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, he embarked on his music career as a <a href="/wiki/Battle_rapper" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle rapper">battle rapper</a>, and later formed a short-lived rap group, The Bloodhoundz. In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>-based rapper <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a> signed Meek Mill to his first record deal. In February 2011, after leaving <a href="/wiki/Grand_Hustle_Records" title="Grand Hustle Records">Grand Hustle Records</a>, Mill signed with Miami-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Maybach_Music_Group" title="Maybach Music Group">Maybach Music Group</a> (MMG). Mill's debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Dreams_and_Nightmares" title="Dreams and Nightmares">Dreams and Nightmares</a></i>, was released in 2012 under MMG and <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>. The album, preceded by the lead single "<a href="/wiki/Amen_(Meek_Mill_song)" title="Amen (Meek Mill song)">Amen</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>), peaked at number two on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.
</p><p>In October 2012, Mill announced the launch of his own <a href="/wiki/Imprint_label" class="mw-redirect" title="Imprint label">label imprint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dream_Chasers_Records" title="Dream Chasers Records">Dream Chasers Records</a>, named after his mixtape series. Meek Mill rose to fame after featured on MMG's <i>Self Made</i> <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation</a>, with his debut singles "<a href="/wiki/Tupac_Back" title="Tupac Back">Tupac Back</a>" (featuring Rick Ross) and "<a href="/wiki/Ima_Boss" class="mw-redirect" title="Ima Boss">Ima Boss</a>" (featuring Rick Ross), being included on <a href="/wiki/Self_Made_Vol._1" title="Self Made Vol. 1">volume one</a> (2011). He released his second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Dreams_Worth_More_Than_Money" title="Dreams Worth More Than Money">Dreams Worth More Than Money</a></i>, in 2015 and his third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Wins_%26_Losses" title="Wins &amp; Losses">Wins &amp; Losses</a></i>, in 2016. His fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Championships_(album)" title="Championships (album)">Championships</a></i>, was released in November 2018 and debuted at the top of the <i>Billboard</i> 200 chart. Its lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Going_Bad" title="Going Bad">Going Bad</a>" (featuring Drake), peaked at number six on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, marking Mill's highest charting single to date. Meek's fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Expensive_Pain" title="Expensive Pain">Expensive Pain</a></i>, was released on October 1, 2021.
</p><p>In November 2017, he was sentenced to two to four years in prison for violating parole, before being released while his trial continues after serving five months. In August 2019, a documentary series about his battle with the criminal justice system, <i><a href="/wiki/Free_Meek" title="Free Meek">Free Meek</a></i>, was released on <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Prime_Video" title="Amazon Prime Video">Amazon Prime Video</a>. Mill served as executive producer on the series alongside fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>. The two also became the co-founders of nonprofit organization <a href="/wiki/Reform_Alliance_(United_States)" title="Reform Alliance (United States)">Reform Alliance</a>, which focuses on national prison reform through <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobbying</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newsweek_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweek-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Robert Rihmeek Williams<sup id="cite_ref-WarnerChappell_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WarnerChappell-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> was born on May 6, 1987,<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/South_Philadelphia" title="South Philadelphia">South Philadelphia</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, the son of Kathy Williams. He has an older sister, Nasheema Williams. Kathy grew up in poverty and her mother died when she was young. Meek's father was killed when Meek was five years old, apparently during an attempted robbery. His uncle, Robert, described Meek Mill's father as a "<a href="/wiki/Black_sheep" title="Black sheep">black sheep</a> of the family". After her husband's death, Kathy moved with Meek and his sister to <a href="/wiki/North_Philadelphia" title="North Philadelphia">North Philadelphia</a>, where they lived in a three-bedroom apartment on Berks Street. Their financial condition was poor and she started cutting hair, doing other jobs, and shoplifting in order to support her family.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> At home, Meek was shy and rarely spoke. As a kid, he became acquainted with another of his father's brothers, who under the MC name Grandmaster Nell was a pioneering <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">disc jockey</a> (DJ) in the late-1980s Philadelphia hip-hop scene and influenced rap artists <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Jazzy_Jeff" title="DJ Jazzy Jeff">DJ Jazzy Jeff</a>. Meek's interest in <a href="/wiki/Hip-hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip-hop">hip-hop</a> grew as a result of these early influences. He was also influenced by the independent hip-hop artists Chic Raw and Vodka, whom he learned to emulate by watching their DVDs.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TheFader_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheFader-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During his early teenage years, Meek often took part in <a href="/wiki/Rap_battle" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap battle">rap battles</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">pseudonym</a> Meek Millz. He often stayed up well past midnight filling notebooks with phrases and verses that he later drew on. Later he and three friends formed the rap group The Bloodhoundz. They bought blank <a href="/wiki/Compact_disc" title="Compact disc">CDs</a> and jewel cases at <a href="/wiki/Kinkos" class="mw-redirect" title="Kinkos">Kinkos</a>, encouraging friends to burn them with the group's songs and distribute them.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="2006.E2.80.932010:_Career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2006–2010:_Career_beginnings">2006–2010: Career beginnings</span></h3>
<p>The Bloodhoundz lasted long enough to release four <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtapes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-background_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-background-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> From 2006 to 2008 Mill released three solo mixtapes including <i>The Real Me</i>, <i>The Real Me 2</i>, and <i>Flamers</i>. In 2009, Mill released his fourth solo mixtape, <i>Flamers 2: Hottest in tha City,</i> which spawned the <a href="/wiki/Promotional_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Promotional single">promotional singles</a> "I'm So Fly," "Prolli," and "Hottest in the City." <i>Flamers 2</i> caught the attention of Charles "Charlie Mack" Alston, founder and president of 215 Aphillyated Records. Mack, who previously represented for other Philadelphians Will Smith, DJ Jazzy Jeff, <a href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men" title="Boyz II Men">Boyz II Men</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ms._Jade" title="Ms. Jade">Ms. Jade</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> was so impressed with Mill that he immediately signed him to his management company. During that same year, Meek Mill also met the founder and owner of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Hustle_Records" title="Grand Hustle Records">Grand Hustle Records</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>-based rapper and record executive <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> T.I. was also impressed by Mill and offered him an opportunity to travel, to meet with him and <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>; within a week both record companies offered him a deal. Although he was offered other record deals, Mill felt collaborating with T.I. was "an opportunity of a lifetime" and thus chose his label. However, a setback occurred, when Mill was sentenced to a stint in jail for a drug and gun charge.<sup id="cite_ref-background_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-background-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After being released in 2009, he continued working as an artist under Grand Hustle, Mill formed a work relationship with the label's resident <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">disc jockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Drama" title="DJ Drama">DJ Drama</a>. Mill and Drama teamed up to release the third edition of Mill's <i>Flamers</i> series. The mixtape, titled <i>Flamers 3: The Wait Is Over</i>, was released on March 12, 2010, and is helmed as a "<a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Grillz" class="mw-redirect" title="Gangsta Grillz">Gangsta Grillz</a> mixtape".<sup id="cite_ref-flamers3_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flamers3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape features his promotional single "Rosé Red", which was later <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remixed</a> with additional <a href="/wiki/Verse_(popular_music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Verse (popular music)">verses</a> from fellow American rappers T.I., <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vado_(rapper)" title="Vado (rapper)">Vado</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-flamers3_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flamers3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Rick Ross contributed his verse after he was visiting Philadelphia and asked his <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> followers who he should collaborate with; Meek Mill was the overwhelming response.<sup id="cite_ref-flamers3_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flamers3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The remix was included on Mill's following mixtape, <i>Mr. Philadelphia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Due to Mill and T.I.'s respective legal troubles, Mill was never able to release an official album under Grand Hustle and they parted ways in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-grandhustle_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grandhustle-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> That same year, a film was released  called <i>Streets</i>. A <a href="/wiki/Direct-to-video" title="Direct-to-video">direct-to-DVD</a> <a href="/wiki/Crime_film" title="Crime film">crime drama</a>, starring Mill, produced by Alston and directed by Jamal Hill.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2011.E2.80.932012:_Dreams_.26_Nightmares"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–2012:_Dreams_&amp;_Nightmares">2011–2012: <i>Dreams &amp; Nightmares</i></span></h3>
<p>In February 2011, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> announced the signing of Mill along with fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Wale_(rapper)" title="Wale (rapper)">Wale</a> to his <a href="/wiki/Maybach_Music_Group" title="Maybach Music Group">Maybach Music Group</a> (MMG) label. In March 2011, Mill was included in <a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)"><i>XXL</i></a>'s "Freshman Class of 2011".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, he released his debut <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">single</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Tupac_Back" title="Tupac Back">Tupac Back</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, from his label's <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation album</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Self_Made_Vol._1" title="Self Made Vol. 1">Self Made Vol. 1</a></i> (2011). That same year he released his second single, "<a href="/wiki/Ima_Boss" class="mw-redirect" title="Ima Boss">Ima Boss</a>", also take from the compilation and featuring Ross. The song was later <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remixed</a>, featuring T.I., <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Birdman (entertainer)">Birdman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khaled" title="DJ Khaled">DJ Khaled</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a> and Rick Ross. The remix charted on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Hot 100</a> and peaked at No. 51, becoming Mill's most successful <a href="/wiki/Promotional_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Promotional single">single</a> at that time. In August 2011, Mill released <i><a href="/wiki/Dreamchasers" title="Dreamchasers">Dreamchasers</a></i>, a well received mixtape featuring his urban hit "House Party" and <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearance" title="Guest appearance">guest appearances</a> from Rick Ross, <a href="/wiki/Yo_Gotti" title="Yo Gotti">Yo Gotti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beanie_Sigel" title="Beanie Sigel">Beanie Sigel</a> among others.
</p><p>In February 2012, <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> listed Meek Mill as the "#7 hottest MC" in their annual "Hottest MCs in the Game" list.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On May 7, 2012, Mill released the <a href="/wiki/Dreamchasers_2" title="Dreamchasers 2">second installment</a> to his <i>Dreamchasers</i> series.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Within six hours of its release on mixtape website DatPiff.com, <i>Dreamchasers 2</i> was downloaded 1.5 million times.<sup id="cite_ref-theglobe_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theglobe-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> On May 10, it was announced Meek Mill signed with <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a> management.<sup id="cite_ref-life+times_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-life+times-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 19, 2012, "<a href="/wiki/Amen_(Meek_Mill_song)" title="Amen (Meek Mill song)">Amen</a>" - originally included on <i>Dreamchasers 2</i>, was released as the lead single from Mill's debut <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" class="mw-redirect" title="Studio album">studio album</a>. Before releasing his debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Dreams_%26_Nightmares" class="mw-redirect" title="Dreams &amp; Nightmares">Dreams &amp; Nightmares</a></i>, Mill received co-signs from both <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, with him appearing on Carey's 2012 single "<a href="/wiki/Triumphant_(Get_%27Em)" title="Triumphant (Get &#39;Em)">Triumphant (Get 'Em)</a>" and the latter stating, "I got my eyes on him. He's the next one to take this shit over." The album was released on October 30, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted at number two on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart with first-week sales of 165,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In its second week, the album sold 41,000 more copies, dropping six spots on the chart to number eight.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.932017:_Dreams_Worth_More_Than_Money.2C_DC4_and_Wins_.26_Losses"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–2017:_Dreams_Worth_More_Than_Money,_DC4_and_Wins_&amp;_Losses">2013–2017: <i>Dreams Worth More Than Money</i>, <i>DC4</i> and <i>Wins &amp; Losses</i></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dreams_Worth_More_Than_Money" title="Dreams Worth More Than Money">Dreams Worth More Than Money</a>, <a href="/wiki/DC4_(mixtape)" title="DC4 (mixtape)">DC4 (mixtape)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wins_%26_Losses" title="Wins &amp; Losses">Wins &amp; Losses</a></div>
<p>Mill released the third installment of the <i>Dreamchasers</i> series, <i><a href="/wiki/Dreamchasers_3" title="Dreamchasers 3">Dreamchasers 3</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-dream3_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dream3-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape featured guest appearances from <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waka_Flocka_Flame" title="Waka Flocka Flame">Waka Flocka Flame</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wale_(rapper)" title="Wale (rapper)">Wale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trina" title="Trina">Trina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-dream3_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dream3-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape was scheduled to be released on May 6, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> However, he had announced that it would be pushed back, eventually to be released on September 29, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In November 2013, Mill announced thathe was half-way finished with his second studio album. On March 8, 2014, Mill announced that the album would be titled <i><a href="/wiki/Dreams_Worth_More_Than_Money" title="Dreams Worth More Than Money">Dreams Worth More Than Money</a></i>. Mill's album, <i>Dreams Worth More Than Money</i>, which was released on June 28, 2015, topped the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> as of the issue dated July 18, 2015.
</p><p>Meek Mill posted 6 videos on his Instagram previewing music for his mixtape, <i>DC4</i>. The mixtape was planned to have featured a remix of his enemy, <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>'s song, "<a href="/wiki/Back_to_Back_(Drake_song)" title="Back to Back (Drake song)">Back to Back</a>", and a remix to Drake and <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>'s song, "I'm the Plug", but unfortunately, due to <i>DC4</i> being released commercially, neither of these two remixes made the final cut.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On January 16, 2016, Meek Mill dropped songs on his <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">extended play</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/4/4_(EP_series)" title="4/4 (EP series)">4/4</a></i>, with 4 tracks. On January 30, 2016, Meek Mill released another extended play title <i>4/4, Pt. 2</i>.
</p><p>Meek Mill released <i><a href="/wiki/DC4_(mixtape)" title="DC4 (mixtape)">DC4</a></i> on October 28, 2016.
</p><p>On July 21, 2017, Mill released his third studio album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Wins_%26_Losses" title="Wins &amp; Losses">Wins &amp; Losses</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.932021:_Championships_and_Expensive_Pain"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–2021:_Championships_and_Expensive_Pain">2018–2021: <i>Championships</i> and <i>Expensive Pain</i></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Championships_(album)" title="Championships (album)">Championships (album)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Expensive_Pain" title="Expensive Pain">Expensive Pain</a></div>
<p>On November 16, 2018, Mill announced his fourth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Championships_(album)" title="Championships (album)">Championships</a></i>, which was released on November 30. The album received positive reviews from critics and debuted atop the US <i>Billboard</i> 200, selling 229,000 <a href="/wiki/Album-equivalent_units" class="mw-redirect" title="Album-equivalent units">album-equivalent units</a> in its first week (42,000 coming from <a href="/wiki/Album_sales" class="mw-redirect" title="Album sales">pure sales</a>).
</p><p>In June 2020, Mill released his <a href="/wiki/Protest_song" title="Protest song">protest song</a> "<a href="/wiki/Otherside_of_America" title="Otherside of America">Otherside of America</a>", amid the <a href="/wiki/George_Floyd_protests" title="George Floyd protests">protests</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Murder_of_George_Floyd" title="Murder of George Floyd">murder of George Floyd</a>.
</p><p>On November 20, 2020, Meek returned with a four-track EP, <i>Quarantine Pack</i>, which features rappers <a href="/wiki/42_Dugg" title="42 Dugg">42 Dugg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vory" title="Vory">Vory</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Durk" title="Lil Durk">Lil Durk</a>, who also appears in the video for the track, "Pain Away". That same month, the film, <i><a href="/wiki/Charm_City_Kings" title="Charm City Kings">Charm City Kings</a></i>, was released exclusively on <a href="/wiki/HBO_Max" class="mw-redirect" title="HBO Max">HBO Max</a>. Originally scheduled for a May 2020 theatrical release by <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures" title="Sony Pictures">Sony Pictures</a>, it was delayed due to the COVID-19 pandemic and later acquired by <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Angel_Manuel_Soto" class="mw-redirect" title="Angel Manuel Soto">Angel Manuel Soto</a>-directed and Will Smith-produced drama stars Mill and opposite Jahi Di'Allo Winston as street bikers who end up under a wave of <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Baltimore" title="Crime in Baltimore">crime in Baltimore</a>. It received positive critical reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> A month earlier, in October, Mill also claimed to have had plans to release an album before the end of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> However, this did not occur, as his fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Expensive_Pain" title="Expensive Pain">Expensive Pain</a></i>, was only released a year later, on October 1, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 after accumulating 95,000 equivalent units.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Mill went on to state that Atlantic Records was responsible for the low sales of the album. He went as afar to state that the label wouldn't allow him to bring <a href="/wiki/PnB_Rock" title="PnB Rock">PnB Rock</a> nor <a href="/wiki/Roddy_Ricch" title="Roddy Ricch">Roddy Ricch</a> as artists to his Dream Chasers imprint,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> while also clarifying that Atlantic restricted him from releasing any more music for the following nine months<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and demanded his release alongside labelmates, fellow Philadelphian <a href="/wiki/Lil_Uzi_Vert" title="Lil Uzi Vert">Lil Uzi Vert</a>, and <a href="/wiki/YoungBoy_Never_Broke_Again" title="YoungBoy Never Broke Again">YoungBoy Never Broke Again</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ourgenerationmusic.com_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourgenerationmusic.com-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 11, 2022, Mill confirmed that he had ended his management deal with Jay-Z's Roc Nation Entertainment, stating that although he and the company are no longer partners in the exact term, he and Jay remain on good terms.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Despite his departure, the two still work on their prison reform venture, the REFORM Alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dream_Chasers_Records">Dream Chasers Records</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dream_Chasers_Records" title="Dream Chasers Records">Dream Chasers Records</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MeekMillPapamitrou_(cropped).png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/MeekMillPapamitrou_%28cropped%29.png/220px-MeekMillPapamitrou_%28cropped%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/MeekMillPapamitrou_%28cropped%29.png/330px-MeekMillPapamitrou_%28cropped%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/MeekMillPapamitrou_%28cropped%29.png/440px-MeekMillPapamitrou_%28cropped%29.png 2x" data-file-width="761" data-file-height="507" /></a><figcaption>Meek Mill (seated) in the studio with <a href="/wiki/Papamitrou" title="Papamitrou">Papamitrou</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>On October 26, 2012, Meek Mill announced the launch of his own record label imprint, <a href="/wiki/Dream_Chasers_Records" title="Dream Chasers Records">Dream Chasers Records</a>, with the flagship artists Louie V. Gutta, Lee Mazin and Goldie.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On July 24, 2019, Meek Mill announced the official launch of Dream Chasers Records as a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a>. Mill spoke on the deal saying "Creating a record label has always been the next step in my journey as a businessman and I appreciate Roc Nation and Jay-Z's support on this new venture. I want to take my experiences in the music industry, use them to find young, hungry talent and open doors for the next generation of artists."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The label also handles its own operations, creative strategy, marketing and business affairs. Jay-Z spoke on the joint venture, saying "Everything he has done leading up to this point shows he is ready to [lead] the next generation. We look at the big picture — this is way beyond signing artists and having hot records."<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> As president of the label, Mill oversees a team in a corporate New York office and also help operate a recording studio for the label's artists.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_proceedings">Criminal proceedings</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2005-2006:_Police_brutality_and_first_arrest">2005-2006: Police brutality and first arrest</span></h4>
<p>When he was 18, while walking to a corner store armed, Meek was arrested for <a href="/wiki/Criminal_possession_of_a_weapon" title="Criminal possession of a weapon">illegally possessing a firearm</a> and was <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality_in_the_United_States" title="Police brutality in the United States">beaten up by the police</a>. Because of the beating, his lips and both eyes became swollen and one of his braids was ripped out. He was charged with attempted or aggravated assault against a police officer after two black cops gave a statement against him in the case, saying he chased them down with a gun and tried to shoot one of them. He was then placed on probation.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TheFader_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheFader-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sun-Times_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sun-Times-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2008:_Drug_and_gun_conviction">2008: Drug and gun conviction</span></h4>
<p>In 2008, Mill was convicted of possession of <a href="/wiki/Drug_paraphernalia" title="Drug paraphernalia">drug paraphernalia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/National_Firearms_Act" title="National Firearms Act">second-degree possession of a loaded firearm by a convicted felon</a>. He was sentenced to eleven to twenty-three months in prison, followed by eight years probation, by <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Philadelphia County, Pennsylvania">Philadelphia County</a> <a href="/wiki/Superior_Court_of_Pennsylvania" title="Superior Court of Pennsylvania">Superior Court</a> Judge Genece Brinkley.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> After Mill's 2008 conviction, Brinkley continued to handle Mill's further legal cases and oversaw his probation. Mill was released in early 2009 under a five-year parole agreement after serving seven months.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-violation_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-violation-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-threat_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-threat-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In January 2023, Pennsylvania governor <a href="/wiki/Tom_Wolf" title="Tom Wolf">Tom Wolf</a> <a href="/wiki/Pardon" title="Pardon">pardoned</a> Mill for these convictions.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2012-2016:_Several_violations.2C_incarceration_and_house_arrest"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012-2016:_Several_violations,_incarceration_and_house_arrest">2012-2016: Several violations, incarceration and house arrest</span></h4>
<p>On the night of <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a> 2012, following an album release party for his debut, <i>Dreams and Nightmares</i>, in South Philadelphia, Mill was detained by <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Police_Department" title="Philadelphia Police Department">city police</a> after a car which he was riding in was pulled over. The outcome of the arrest remains unknown; no charges were filed, and Mill was released from custody.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> However, in December, because of the incident, Mill was found to have violated his probation for his 2008 federal drug and gun charges, resulting in Judge Brinkley revoking Mill's travel permit.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2013, Mill was again found to have violated his probation and ordered to take etiquette classes. The violation was a failure to report travel plans as required and social media postings that resulted in death threats to the probation officer who assigned his case.<sup id="cite_ref-violation_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-violation-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In requiring the classes and stressing the requirement to report travel, Brinkley noted, "You need to try to get this right next time."<sup id="cite_ref-threat_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-threat-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In June 2013, the court noted that Mill continually failed to report his travel plans. Brinkley established an August deadline for the classes, noting that Mill has "a lot of issues" and that the classes would provide him with a "big-picture perspective" on his personal and professional actions. Brinkley said the classes were "more important than any concerts he might have."<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Of the requirement to provide travel plans to his probation officer, Mill complained, "You just gonna miss money all day." The ADA explained that it was a consequence of being on probation.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On July 11, 2014, Mill's probation was revoked and he was sentenced to three to six months in jail.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> He was released on December 2, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was found guilty for a parole violation again on December 17, 2015, due to him performing at an <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> show for Nicki Minaj's <a href="/wiki/The_Pinkprint_Tour" title="The Pinkprint Tour"><i>Pinkprint</i> tour</a>, the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards_2015" title="BET Awards 2015">2015 BET Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2015" title="American Music Awards of 2015">American Music Awards</a> respectively, all without reporting his actions as related court orders to gain approval.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The judge hearing his case refused to give him a second chance and ordered him not to work or perform before his sentencing on February 5, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> He was sentenced to 90 days of <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a> on February 5. The sentence became effective on March 1. Mill was not allowed to work and was required to do daily community service with groups serving adults. He was also sentenced to an extended six years probation.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On June 2, 2016, Mill was sentenced to eight additional days of house arrest as a result of him not completing his required community service hours.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> His house arrest ended fifteen days later.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2017:_St._Louis_and_New_York_arrests.3B_parole_violation_and_imprisonment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017:_St._Louis_and_New_York_arrests;_parole_violation_and_imprisonment">2017: St. Louis and New York arrests; parole violation and imprisonment</span></h4>
<p>On March 11, 2017, Mill was arrested at the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a> <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Lambert_International_Airport" title="St. Louis Lambert International Airport">Lambert International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a> for assaulting two employees. Shortly after his arrest, he was given a court summons.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Then, in August, he was detained in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> after a noise complaint was filed over Mill popping a wheelie on his motorcycle. Soon after, he was released once the <a href="/wiki/Noise_reduction" title="Noise reduction">disturbance</a> violation and reckless driving charges were dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The case was later taken to court in October, and was to be dismissed if Mill would have completed six months of therapy, resulting in good behavior and thirty hours of community service added to his Pennsylvania-state related twenty-hour term.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> On November 6, 2017, he was sentenced to two to four years in state prison for violating his parole. He served five months at the <a href="/wiki/State_Correctional_Institution_%E2%80%93_Chester" title="State Correctional Institution – Chester">State Correctional Institution – Chester</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chester,_Pennsylvania" title="Chester, Pennsylvania">Chester, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 24, 2018, Mill was released, pending outcome of an appeal to the Pennsylvania supreme court.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The Philadelphia district attorney petitioned Brinkley for his release, citing credibility issues with the arresting officer in his initial 2008 conviction.<sup id="cite_ref-tmz_da_moves_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tmz_da_moves-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Brinkley declined and instead scheduled the case for a hearing.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Hours after his release from prison, <a href="/wiki/Michael_G._Rubin" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael G. Rubin">Michael G. Rubin</a>, a minority owner of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers" title="Philadelphia 76ers">Philadelphia 76ers</a> and longtime supporter of Mill, flew Mill in by helicopter to a 76ers game to perform a ceremonial bell-ringing on the court.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Garnering support from other public figures such as Jay-Z and fellow Philadelphian <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Hart" title="Kevin Hart">Kevin Hart</a>, Mill has said that he would like to use his situation to "shine a light" on the criminal justice system.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 24, 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Superior_Court_of_Pennsylvania" title="Superior Court of Pennsylvania">Superior Court of Pennsylvania</a> granted Mill's appeal, overturning his 2008 conviction and ordering a new trial to be overseen by another judge other than Judge Brinkley. In a statement, the Philadelphia District Attorney's Office said it was pleased that the appeals court "validated our position that Robert Rihmeek Williams deserves a new trial before a court that has no appearance of partiality." However, the D.A. declined comment on its plans for a new trial, stating the office was weighing its options before proceeding.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2018:_Allegations_of_federal_corruption">2018: Allegations of federal corruption</span></h4>
<p>Reports alleged that there was an FBI investigation into the conduct of Brinkley, the judge presiding over his case. This was later publicly acknowledged by Mill's defense team.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Mill's attorney, Joe Tacopina, made several allegations of inappropriate statements and actions by Brinkley, including that "she requested he re-record a <a href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men" title="Boyz II Men">Boyz II Men</a> song and shout her out, and how she wanted him to leave [the management of] Roc Nation to sign with a friend of hers", referring to Mill's former partner, Charlie Mack of 215 Aphillyated,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and that "she showed up at his community service" when a typical judge would not, among several other irregularities.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2018, the officer of Mill's original 2007 case was brought under scrutiny for the potential mishandling of his arrest. This came upon a whistle-blower's testimony responsible for the revelation of hundreds of other corrupt officers. An appeal to reverse Mill's conviction was submitted.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With Mill's continuous arrests and probation from Brinkley, he is estimated by his booking agency and management to have lost millions of dollars in profit.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2019:_Misdemeanor_firearm_charge_and_Free_Meek">2019: Misdemeanor firearm charge and <i>Free Meek</i></span></h4>
<p>In August 2019, Mill pleaded guilty to a misdemeanor firearm charge in Philadelphia. All other charges were dismissed, officially ending the case against Mill from 2007 and temporarily dismissing him as a convicted felon.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 9, 2019, a docuseries <i><a href="/wiki/Free_Meek" title="Free Meek">Free Meek</a></i> premiered on <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Prime_Video" title="Amazon Prime Video">Amazon Prime Video</a>. The five-part series was produced by Roc Nation, with Mill and Jay-Z serving as executive producers.<sup id="cite_ref-newsweek_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweek-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_suits">Civil suits</span></h3>
<p>On November 29, 2017, Meek Mill and <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a> were sued by the family of Jaquan Graves, who was shot and killed in the parking lot outside a Connecticut concert in December 2016. Graves had just left the facility when gunfire started and he was killed. The lawsuit also claims that Mill and Roc Nation allowed "thugs" to remain on the premises after exhibiting disorderly, disruptive, argumentative, angry and agitated behaviors toward patrons.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_against_Cosmopolitan_Resort">Allegations against Cosmopolitan Resort</span></h3>
<p>In May 2019, Meek Mill was turned away from the <a href="/wiki/Cosmopolitan_of_Las_Vegas" title="Cosmopolitan of Las Vegas">Cosmopolitan of Las Vegas</a> when attempting to attend a show. His attorney, Joe Tacopina, alleged that Mill was turned away because of his race. On May 25, 2019, Mill said that he intended to pursue legal action against the hotel for racial discrimination.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Within days, the Cosmopolitan issued the requested apology. Tacopina then announced that his client had accepted it, and no lawsuit would be forthcoming.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy_and_activism">Philanthropy and activism</span></h2>
<p>In 2016, Meek Mill spent $50,000 to donate 60,000 <a href="/wiki/Ice_Mountain_(water)" title="Ice Mountain (water)">Ice Mountain</a> brand <a href="/wiki/Bottled_water" title="Bottled water">bottled water</a> to contribute to and support the <a href="/wiki/Flint_water_crisis" title="Flint water crisis">Flint water crisis</a> in <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a> as he teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, following his release from state custody, Mill immediately became a leading advocate of <a href="/wiki/Criminal_justice_reform_in_the_United_States" title="Criminal justice reform in the United States">criminal justice reform in the United States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> where he transitioned his advocacy into the co-formation of Reform Alliance with fellow recording artist and entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The nonprofit organization states its mission is "to dramatically reduce the number of people who are unjustly under the control of the criminal justice system – starting with probation and parole",<sup id="cite_ref-REFORM._&#123;&#123;!&#125;&#125;_Reform_Alliance_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REFORM._{{!}}_Reform_Alliance-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> where it plans on doing so by gathering leaders from various fields such as business, entertainment, government, sports, technology, and more, who have the common interest of donating and advocating for criminal justice reform in the United States. Later, in August 2018, Mill donated 6,000 backpacks to students of Philadelphia.
</p><p>The founding partners of Reform Alliance, besides Meek Mill and Jay-Z, includes <a href="/wiki/Kraft_Group" title="Kraft Group">Kraft Group</a> CEO and <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> owner <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kraft" title="Robert Kraft">Robert Kraft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers" title="Philadelphia 76ers">Philadelphia 76ers</a> owner <a href="/wiki/Michael_G._Rubin" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael G. Rubin">Michael G. Rubin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets" title="Brooklyn Nets">Brooklyn Nets</a> co-owner <a href="/wiki/Clara_Wu_Tsai" title="Clara Wu Tsai">Clara Wu Tsai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vista_Equity_Partners" title="Vista Equity Partners">Vista Equity Partners</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Smith_(investor)" title="Robert F. Smith (investor)">Robert F. Smith</a>, as well as other leaders in business, law and politics, whom have collectively pledged a total 50 million dollars to the foundation as of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> To lead the organization, Reform hired political activist, and <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> host/political analyst <a href="/wiki/Van_Jones" title="Van Jones">Van Jones</a> as their inaugural CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-REFORM._&#123;&#123;!&#125;&#125;_Reform_Alliance_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REFORM._{{!}}_Reform_Alliance-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span></h2>
<h3><span id=".22Amen.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Amen&quot;">"Amen"</span></h3>
<p>Following the release of the lead single for <i>Dreams &amp; Nightmares</i>, entitled "<a href="/wiki/Amen_(Meek_Mill_song)" title="Amen (Meek Mill song)">Amen</a>", Philadelphia area pastor Rev. Jomo K. Johnson called for a boycott of Mill due to the song's lyrical content. "As a hip-hop fan, I want to encourage every rap fan in Philadelphia who is a believer in Jesus Christ, to boycott Meek Mill until he acknowledges this blatant disrespect. And being a resident of North Philadelphia and a pastor, I revoke Meek's 'hood pass' until this happens," Johnson said in a statement.
</p><p>On July 17, 2012, in an interview on the <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a> show <i><a href="/wiki/106_%26_Park" title="106 &amp; Park">106 &amp; Park</a></i>, Mill stated, "I don't think no preacher or no church approves of any type of rap music—because rap music, period, is a lot of bad stuff said. But at the end of the day, it's real life. And me, I wasn't trying to disrespect no religion or anything like that."<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feuds">Feuds</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cassidy">Cassidy</span></h4>
<p>A feud started between Meek Mill and fellow Philadelphia-born rapper <a href="/wiki/Cassidy_(rapper)" title="Cassidy (rapper)">Cassidy</a>, when Mill offered to <a href="/wiki/Rap_battle" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap battle">battle</a> several underground rappers including Cassidy. Cassidy would later accept the challenge, adding "if the money was right". They participated in a short social exchange, after which Cassidy released "The Diary of a Hustla", which was originally thought to be a <a href="/wiki/Diss_track" class="mw-redirect" title="Diss track">diss track</a> towards Mill. This was later refuted by Cassidy.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> They both asked $100,000 each for the battle to take place.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> However, after Meek Mill dissed Cassidy's song, "Condom Style" (a remake of <a href="/wiki/Psy" title="Psy">Psy</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Gangnam_Style" title="Gangnam Style">Gangnam Style</a>"), Cassidy released a formal diss track towards Mill with "Me, Myself &amp; iPhone".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Afterwards, Meek Mill responded with the diss track "Repo", which Mill later said would be the final diss record he would release against Cassidy.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cassidy later said the feud was not personal, saying it was all in the spirit of <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> On January 6, 2013, Cassidy released a 10-minute-long diss response titled "Raid".<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Eight months later, on September 5, 2013, Meek Mill released another diss record towards Cassidy, titled "Kendrick You Next". This was despite the fact that he said "Repo" would be his final diss record.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, Cassidy released a diss record titled "Catch A Body", as a response.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> By 2017, the two rappers had resolved their differences.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Drake">Drake</span></h4>
<p>In July 2015, Meek Mill publicly criticized <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canadian</a> Toronto-based entertainer <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a> on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, calling him out for not writing his own lyrics. In a series of tweets, the rapper claimed his counterpart used a <a href="/wiki/Ghostwriter" title="Ghostwriter">ghostwriter</a> for "<a href="/wiki/R.I.C.O._(song)" title="R.I.C.O. (song)">R.I.C.O.</a>", a song off Mill's second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Dreams_Worth_More_Than_Money" title="Dreams Worth More Than Money">Dreams Worth More Than Money</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> He also admitted that he was upset that Drake did not promote the album on Twitter, upon its release. "Stop comparing [me to] Drake. He don't write his own raps. That's why he ain't tweet my album because we found out!", Meek Mill commented.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Meek Mill had identified the <a href="/wiki/Ghostwriter" title="Ghostwriter">ghostwriter</a> as Quentin Miller, a local rapper from Atlanta. Meek Mill's claims received support from <a href="/wiki/Funkmaster_Flex" title="Funkmaster Flex">Funkmaster Flex</a>, an American hip hop DJ on New York City's <a href="/wiki/Hot_97" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot 97">Hot 97</a> radio station. Flex released multiple audio recordings of reference tracks featuring Quentin Miller performing the soon-to-be Drake songs, "10 Bands", "Used To", "Know Yourself" and his guest verse on "R.I.C.O."<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Drake was later supported by his long-time friend, collaborator and co-founder of <a href="/wiki/OVO_Sound" title="OVO Sound">OVO Sound</a>, award-winning multi-platinum selling producer <a href="/wiki/Noah_%2240%22_Shebib" class="mw-redirect" title="Noah &quot;40&quot; Shebib">Noah "40" Shebib</a>, who claimed that not only does Drake write his own songs, he has also written number-one records for other artists. "No one is as talented as Drake… [there are] countless number ones and songs Drake has written for others never mind himself", 40 said on Twitter.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 25, 2015, Drake premiered a track, titled "<a href="/wiki/Charged_Up" title="Charged Up">Charged Up</a>" on the Beats 1 OVO Radio Show that is widely seen as a response to Meek Mill's allegations. Drake highlighted Meek Mill's relatively low sales volume and further claimed that the rapper was fading into obscurity.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Drake also dissed Funkmaster Flex by promoting his rival <a href="/wiki/DJ_Clue%3F" class="mw-redirect" title="DJ Clue?">DJ Clue?</a>. On July 29, Drake released an aggressive diss track, named "<a href="/wiki/Back_to_Back_(Drake_song)" title="Back to Back (Drake song)">Back to Back</a>", that further attacked Meek Mill. The track, streamed over 500,000 times in 4 hours, heavily suggested that Mill's relationship with <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> is lopsided in the latter's favor and also further criticized the former for not responding to "Charged Up" and for only relying on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> to attack Drake.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The track was released for streaming on the OVO SoundCloud account and on <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music" title="Apple Music">Apple Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The next day, Meek Mill released a track attacking Drake titled "<a href="/wiki/Wanna_Know_(Meek_Mill_song)" title="Wanna Know (Meek Mill song)">Wanna Know</a>" through Funkmaster Flex on Hot 97.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> On "Wanna Know", Meek Mill revealed another reference track, ghostwritten by Quentin Miller for Drake, who he criticized for being soft.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Meek Mill also dissed <a href="/wiki/AR-Ab" title="AR-Ab">AR-Ab</a> on the track,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> and claimed that Drake was urinated on inside a movie theatre. Mill then removed the song from <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a> and said that he was moving on from his feud with Drake after WWE sent him a <a href="/wiki/Cease_and_desist" title="Cease and desist">cease and desist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 30, 2016, Drake released a new diss track aimed at Mill, titled "<a href="/wiki/Summer_Sixteen" title="Summer Sixteen">Summer Sixteen</a>", as the <a href="/wiki/Buzz_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Buzz single">buzz single</a>, used to promote his fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Views_(album)" title="Views (album)">Views</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Less than fifteen minutes later, Mill released a response track with his cousin and label mate <a href="/wiki/Omelly" class="mw-redirect" title="Omelly">Omelly</a> called "<a href="/wiki/War_Pain" title="War Pain">War Pain</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The track references several lines from "Summer Sixteen", including an incident in which Drake played "Back to Back" in a public hotel, in which, he had a room directly above Mill. Four months later, Mill released a remix of <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Remy_Ma" title="Remy Ma">Remy Ma</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/All_the_Way_Up_(Fat_Joe_and_Remy_Ma_song)" title="All the Way Up (Fat Joe and Remy Ma song)">All the Way Up</a>" with fellow rappers <a href="/wiki/Fabolous" title="Fabolous">Fabolous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a>. Meek directly references Drake in several lines of the song, such as "If you didn't write it, don't record it." He also implied that he was in a relationship with Drake's current love interest, <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Meek Mill and Drake were both respectively endorsed by <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whataburger" title="Whataburger">Whataburger</a> for their feud.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Mill's release from prison in 2018, the feud was officially squashed. Drake was featured on Mill's song "Going Bad", from his post-incarceration album <i>Championships</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Game">The Game</span></h4>
<p>On September 16, 2016, <a href="/wiki/The_Game_(rapper)" title="The Game (rapper)">The Game</a> released a five-minute freestyle, "92 Bars", which was rumored to be a diss towards Meek Mill.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Previously, Mill and Game collaborated on 2015's "The Soundtrack".<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Hours after the release of "92 Bars", Game admitted that the freestyle was specifically a diss towards Mill. The next day, the two rappers ended up in an <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> exchange, with The Game cyber-flirting with Meek Mill's girlfriend, Nicki Minaj, as well as accusing Mill of informing the authorities of a robbery involving <a href="/wiki/Sean_Kingston" title="Sean Kingston">Sean Kingston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> On September 18 Meek Mill released a diss track toward Game, a remix to <a href="/wiki/Young_M.A" title="Young M.A">Young M.A</a>.'s "<a href="/wiki/Ooouuu" title="Ooouuu">Ooouuu</a>" with Omelly and fellow Philadelphia-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Beanie_Sigel" title="Beanie Sigel">Beanie Sigel</a>. Two days later, The Game responded with "Pest Control", using the same beat and sending shots at Meek Mill, Omelly, Beanie Sigel, and Sean Kingston.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In 2018 the two reconciled after Mill's incarceration and subsequent release from prison.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beanie_Sigel">Beanie Sigel</span></h4>
<p>A dispute between Meek Mill and Beanie Sigel ensued on September 26, 2016, when the latter ridiculed the former's intelligence towards him through a radio interview.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Minutes after the interview, Sigel was punched on the back of his head by someone who was believed to have been one of Meek Mill's affiliates.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Three days later Mill criticized Sigel through many derogatory Instagram messages.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Later Mill dissed Sigel, The Game and Drake in a freestyle on <a href="/wiki/Funkmaster_Flex" title="Funkmaster Flex">Funkmaster Flex</a>'s radio show.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Sigel responded by releasing a diss track titled "I'm Coming".<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In November 2018, Sigel supported Mill's album, <i>Championships</i>, stating there were "no skips" on the album, assumably ending the dispute between the two.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="6ix9ine">6ix9ine</span></h4>
<p>In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Power_106" class="mw-redirect" title="Power 106">Power 106</a> in November 2018, when Meek Mill was asked about rapper <a href="/wiki/6ix9ine" title="6ix9ine">6ix9ine</a>, who <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_the_Nine_Trey_Gangsters" title="Trial of the Nine Trey Gangsters">was arrested</a> on <a href="/wiki/Racket_(crime)" class="mw-redirect" title="Racket (crime)">racketeering</a>, weapons and drugs charges earlier that month, he spoke about wanting to warn him of the consequences of his antics.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In January 2019, after it was revealed that 6ix9ine would be cooperating with prosecutors, Meek tweeted that he already predicted that 6ix9ine would do so,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and would continually diss him for that. After 6ix9ine was released earlier from prison in 2020, he and Mill continued to take shots at each other; at one time Mill called 6ix9ine's song "<a href="/wiki/Gooba" title="Gooba">Gooba</a>" "trash".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In June 2020, 6ix9ine criticized Mill for releasing his protest song, "Otherside of America", while not "protesting".<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>  On February 14, 2021, the rappers got into an altercation outside an Atlanta club, in which 6ix9ine clowned Mill for having security around him and lunged at them, but was stopped by Mill's security. Both rappers posted videos of the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> On February 19, 2021, 6ix9ine released a diss track towards Mill, titled "<a href="/wiki/Zaza_(song)" title="Zaza (song)">Zaza</a>", with a music video that includes a clip of the altercation.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> In response, Mill issued a <a href="/wiki/Cease_and_desist" title="Cease and desist">cease and desist</a> to 6ix9ine.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_feuds">Other feuds</span></h4>
<p>In August 2013, Mill was one of the many rappers mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a> on his guest verse on Big Sean's "<a href="/wiki/Control_(Big_Sean_song)" title="Control (Big Sean song)">Control</a>". Lamar touted himself as the king of both <a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">coasts</a> and threatened to "murder" the rappers he mentioned, despite being associated with them before.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> During a performance at a music festival in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, Mill sent derogatory messages to Lamar.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> On September 9, 2013, Mill later released "Ooh, Kill 'Em", a response to Lamar's verse on "Control".<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2013, Mill instigated an argument on social media with fellow Maybach Music Group artist Wale for not backing him up in his feud with Cassidy, despite the fact that Cassidy had dissed Wale and several others Meek and Wale were affiliated with. He also criticized Wale for not helping him support his second studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Two years later their dispute reignited after Wale sided with Drake over Mill during their high-profile feud.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The following year, after a long talk with their mentor Rick Ross, Mill and Wale ended their feud and released a duet, "Make It Work", on July 8, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mill's dispute with AR-Ab ensued after the former's rival, Drake, referenced the latter on his song "Back to Back", saying, "I waited four days, nigga, where y'all at? I drove here in the Wraith playin' AR-Ab." AR-Ab appeared on VladTV in August 2015, said he had not signed to Drake's <a href="/wiki/OVO_Sound" title="OVO Sound">OVO Sound</a>, and sided with him. He was also disappointed at Mill's response, since he called out AR-Ab on "Wanna Know", the response to Drake's diss track. On August 6, during a performance at the <a href="/wiki/BB%26T_Pavilion" class="mw-redirect" title="BB&amp;T Pavilion">BB&amp;T Pavilion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">Camden, New Jersey</a>, Mill responded, "fuck AR-Ab" and questioned his allegiance to an out-of-town rapper. AR-Ab responded by releasing his own version of "Back to Back" on August 8, which disses Mill and also contains violent lyrics threatening to unleash his "shooters" on Mill.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In response, Meek's cousin and Dream Chasers signee Omelly released his own version of "Back to Back" that dissed AR-Ab. AR-Ab did another interview on VladTV and said Mill was too scared to respond himself and Omelly was the "softest one on Dream Chasers". He also said he would not respond to Omelly's diss because he was a "worker".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> In January 2016 AR-Ab revealed that he and Mill had talked it out and their feud was now over.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 25, 2016, Mill dissed his record label boss Rick Ross's long-time nemesis, <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>, on his <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">extended play</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/4/4_(EP_series)" title="4/4 (EP series)">4/4</a></i> (not counting the remix to Drake and <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>'s "I'm the Plug").<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> After hearing the EP, 50 Cent replied with a set of over 22 <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">memes</a>, including one where he said that he should run to his girlfriend at the time, Nicki Minaj, and cry to her.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Mill disparaged 50 in a direct message, ridiculing his case involving Ross's ex-girlfriend, followed up by his bankruptcy case.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> On January 30, 2016, Mill dissed 50 again on "War Pain", in the middle of his verse, saying, "My Philly boys will creep up on you when you ain't looking, with your little memes."<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The next day, 50 and several members of his group, <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>, counter-dissed Mill at a concert.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The conflict between Mill and 50 also reignited the feud between 50 and Ross.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On June 30, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Budden" title="Joe Budden">Joe Budden</a> dissed Mill and Drake on "Making a Murderer, Pt. 1", a counter-diss to Drake's "4PM in Calabasas", as well as on his guest verse to <a href="/wiki/French_Montana" title="French Montana">French Montana</a>'s "No Shopping".<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Following his release from his three-to-six month prison sentence for probation violation on December 2, 2014, Mill began dating rapper and singer Nicki Minaj in early 2015; he accompanied her as an opening act on her 2015 world tour.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> On January 2, 2017, it was reported that Mill and Minaj had ended their two-year relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Their breakup is furthermore detailed on Minaj's 2017 single, "<a href="/wiki/Regret_in_Your_Tears" title="Regret in Your Tears">Regret in Your Tears</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> While shopping in Maxfield in early 2020, Mill was involved in a verbal altercation with Minaj and her husband, Kenneth Petty, before he was escorted out of the store. The issue resulted in a Twitter exchange between Mill and Minaj, highlighting a series of abuse allegations by both parties.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mill has three children. In 2020, Mill's then-girlfriend, Milan Rouge, gave birth to his third child, and her first, on the rapper's 33rd birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-3rd_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3rd-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
